<span id="vii.iii"></span>

## <span id="vii.iii-p0.1"></span>Index of Greek Words and Phrases

<span id="vii.iii-p0.3"></span>

<span class="Greek"> [1. That Christ entered into the rest which He
promised His people, while Moses did not. 2. That that rest is Heaven,
not the earthly Canaan.](1140105.htm#v.xi-p26.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [As the text stands we must suppose that he is
alluding to sayings which had become proverbial, and that his hearers
would supply the words,](1140123.htm#v.xxix-p42.9.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Below Morel.
reads,](1140037.htm#iv.xxxiv-p44.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [But the three mss.](1140114.htm#v.xx-p40.9.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Cf. in 1 Cor. Hom. v. § 4, p. 56, Oxf.
Tr.](1140099.htm#v.v-p33.4.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Dr. Bright, Hist. of Church, between
a.d.](1140131.htm#v.xxxvii-p94.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Field.](1140125.htm#v.xxxi-p33.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Four of the six
mss.](1140120.htm#v.xxvi-p36.8.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [G. T.](1140091.htm#iv.lxxxviii-p56.6.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [If therefore it is
acknowledged,](1140063.htm#iv.lx-p70.4.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [It means rejected after testing, as in case of
metals: which may take place, as St. Chrys. implies in this passage,
either here or hereafter; either for a time or for
eternity.](1140108.htm#v.xiv-p9.20.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Mr. Field prefers leaving it as it stands without
conjecturing what is omitted: only observing that the
words](1140115.htm#v.xxi-p48.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Mr. Field thinks that neither reading gives a
suitable meaning. If the reading adopted by Mr. F. and followed in the
translation be the true one, it must be supposed that St. Chrys. had in
mind the condition in which Ezra, or perhaps Nehemiah, found the Jews.
The words](1140112.htm#v.xviii-p51.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [N.T.](1140093.htm#iv.xc-p47.2.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [N.T. ](1140069.htm#iv.lxvi-p45.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Of the use of](1140099.htm#v.v-p32.6.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Perhaps this may be the true reading, St Chrys. in
these words turning his address to those who are suffering worldly
wrong: and saying that if they patiently endure, they are not the
sufferers, but inflict suffering on their oppressors, though the
expression](1140123.htm#v.xxix-p34.4.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [See Hom. xxvii. \[6\], pp. 489
sqq.](1140120.htm#v.xxvi-p28.6.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [See St. Chrys. Homily on the words, John xvii.
19](1140115.htm#v.xxi-p36.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [See many instances of its use in this sense in Mr.
Field’s note on St. Chrys. on 1 Cor. Hom. xxviii. (p. 255, A). \[See p.
390, O.T.\]](1140098.htm#v.iv-p61.2.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [St. C. makes this the order of the narrative, but
most commentators refer the words to an earlier
period.](1140088.htm#iv.lxxxv-p70.8.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [St. Chrys. alludes to these words in what follows:
but without citing them.](1140111.htm#v.xvii-p42.6.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [St. Chrys. however is speaking of a bishop who
repeats baptism.](1140107.htm#v.xiii-p46.6.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [St. Chrys.
substitutes](1140110.htm#v.xvi-p34.16.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [The Bened. translator
has](1140120.htm#v.xxvi-p42.10.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [The Greek has simply the adjective and noun which
would naturally be connected by the simple
copula.—F.G.\]](1140131.htm#v.xxxvii-p15.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [The introduction of
the](1140112.htm#v.xviii-p47.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [The literal sense is
either](1140092.htm#iv.lxxxix-p60.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [The readings here vary, without variety of
meaning.](1140048.htm#iv.xlv-p37.6.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [There are many other instances of a similar
negligence of style in the genuine text, as also in other works of St.
Chrys.](1140107.htm#v.xiii-p54.9.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [This he applies to the Christian keeping guard
over himself (his words are](1140110.htm#v.xvi-p34.24.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [This looks like the gloss of a transcriber,
surprised at the suspension of the
sense.](1140047.htm#iv.xliv-p55.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [Whether](1140130.htm#v.xxxvi-p7.7.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [\[](1140114.htm#v.xx-p7.2)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [\[It is the same word as above and is rendered in
the R.V.](1140128.htm#v.xxxiv-p20.2.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [\[The passage is,](1140101.htm#v.vii-p43.9.md)</span>

<span class="Greek"> [\[There seems to be no need of this slight
correction; the present participle of the Greek is even more closely
represented by the A.V. than by the above translation. But in view of
this note, it must be allowed to
stand.—F.G.\]](1140108.htm#v.xiv-p4.7.md)</span>

word](1140107.htm#v.xiii-p18.5.md)</span>

The word](1140100.htm#v.vi-p33.7.md)</span>

<span class="Greek">[ N.T.](1140093.htm#iv.xc-p12.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek">[ One ms.](1140090.htm#iv.lxxxvii-p90.3.md)</span>

<span class="Greek">[The inclining of the

<span class="Greek">[The large proportion of quotations from the Psalms
in this Epistle is noticed in the article upon it in Smith’s Bible
Dictionary (where the proportion is stated as 16 out of 32); but my
attention was first called to the bearing of this upon the question of
authorship by the quick observation of Rev. Hermann Lilienthal. It is
not easy to give a precise numerical statement of the proportion because
of the large number of historical allusions which can hardly be reckoned
as quotations, and also because the New Testament writers often clothe
their thoughts in the familiar words of the Old Testament, apparently
without any conscious quotation. This matter, however, which cannot be
tabulated, is quite in accord with the rest, and the whole Epistle is
saturated with the language and the historical allusions of the Psalms.
Taking only what may fairly be considered as designed quotations, the
relative numbers taken from the Psalms are:  Hebrews, 200; St. Luke, 25;
St. Paul, 39; all others, 25. The Apocalypse is omitted from the
calculation. In the comparatively few quotations in St. Luke less than
one-third (17 out of 55) are from the Psalms, and every one of these in
recording the words of others; less than one-fifth in St. Paul (16 out
of 89); and in the others 22 out of 116. In Hebrews almost exactly
one-half.](1140097.htm#v.iii-p129.1.md)</span>

but cast lots for it, whose it shall be, that the Scripture might be
fulfilled which saith, They parted My raiment among them, and for My
vesture they did cast lots.](1140090.htm#iv.lxxxvii-p20.4.md)</span>

<span class="Greek">[Then those men, when they had seen the miracle that
Jesus did, said, This is of a truth that Prophet which should come into
the world.](1140047.htm#iv.xliv-p71.5.md)</span>

<span class="Greek">[Then took Mary a pound of ointment of spikenard,

pence, and given to the poor? This he said, not that he cared for the

therein.](1140070.htm#iv.lxvii-p33.4.md)</span>
